CHAPTER THIRTY CONSEQUENCES Mrs. Chester 's fair be so very elegant and select that it be consider a great honor by the young lady of the neighborhood to be invite to take a table , and everyone be much interested in the matter .

CHAPTER THIRTY-ONE OUR FOREIGN CORRESPONDENT London Dearest People , Here I really sit at a front window of the Bath Hotel , Piccadilly .
It 's not a fashionable place , but Uncle stop here year ago , and wo n't go anywhere else .
However , we do n't mean to stay long , so it 's no great matter .
Oh , I ca n't begin to tell you how I enjoy it all !
I never can , so I 'll only give you bits out of my notebook , for I 've do nothing but sketch and scribble since I start .
I send a line from Halifax , when I felt pretty miserable , but after that I get on delightfully , seldom ill , on deck all day , with plenty of pleasant people to amuse me .
Everyone be very kind to me , especially the officer .
Do n't laugh , Jo , gentleman really be very necessary aboard ship , to hold on to , or to wait upon one , and a they have nothing to do , it 's a mercy to make them useful , otherwise they would smoke themselves to death , I 'm afraid .
Aunt and Flo be poorly all the way , and like to be let alone , so when I have do what I could for them , I go and enjoy myself .
Such walk on deck , such sunset , such splendid air and wave !
It be almost as exciting a rid a fast horse , when we go rush on so grandly .
I wish Beth could have come , it would have do her so much good .
As for Jo , she would have go up and sit on the maintop jib , or whatever the high thing be call , make friend with the engineer , and toot on the captain 's speaking trumpet , she 'd have be in such a state of rapture .
It be all heavenly , but I be glad to see the Irish coast , and find it very lovely , so green and sunny , with brown cabin here and there , ruin on some of the hill , and gentleman 's countryseat in the valley , with deer feeding in the park .
It be early in the morning , but I do n't regret get up to see it , for the bay be full of little boat , the shore so picturesque , and a rosy sky overhead .
I never shall forget it .
At Queenstown one of my new acquaintance leave u , Mr. Lennox , and when I say something about the Lakes of Killarney , he sigh , and sung , with a look at me ... `` Oh , have you e'er hear of Kate Kearney ?
She live on the bank of Killarney ; From the glance of her eye , Shun danger and fly , For fatal 's the glance of Kate Kearney . ''
Was n't that nonsensical ?
We only stop at Liverpool a few hour .
It 's a dirty , noisy place , and I be glad to leave it .
Uncle rush out and buy a pair of dogskin glove , some ugly , thick shoe , and an umbrella , and get shave à la mutton chop , the first thing .
Then he flatter himself that he look like a true Briton , but the first time he have the mud clean off his shoe , the little bootblack know that an American stood in them , and say , with a grin , `` There yer har , sir .
I 've give 'em the late Yankee shine . ''
It amuse Uncle immensely .
Oh , I must tell you what that absurd Lennox do !
He get his friend Ward , who come on with u , to order a bouquet for me , and the first thing I saw in my room be a lovely one , with `` Robert Lennox 's compliment , '' on the card .
Was n't that fun , girl ?
I like travel .
I never shall get to London if I do n't hurry .
The trip be like rid through a long picture gallery , full of lovely landscape .
The farmhouse be my delight , with thatched roof , ivy up to the eaves , latticed window , and stout woman with rosy child at the door .
The very cattle look more tranquil than ours , a they stand knee-deep in clover , and the hen have a contented cluck , a if they never get nervous like Yankee biddy .
Such perfect color I never saw , the grass so green , sky so blue , grain so yellow , wood so dark , I be in a rapture all the way .
So be Flo , and we keep bounce from one side to the other , try to see everything while we be whisk along at the rate of sixty mile an hour .
Aunt be tire and go to sleep , but Uncle read his guidebook , and would n't be astonish at anything .
This be the way we go on .
Amy , fly up -- `` Oh , that must be Kenilworth , that gray place among the tree ! ''
Flo , dart to my window -- `` How sweet !
We must go there sometime , wo n't we Papa ? ''
Uncle , calmly admire his boot -- `` No , my dear , not unless you want beer , that 's a brewery . ''
A pause -- then Flo cry out , `` Bless me , there 's a gallows and a man go up . ''
`` Where , where ? ''
shriek Amy , star out at two tall post with a crossbeam and some dangling chain .
`` A colliery , '' remark Uncle , with a twinkle of the eye .
`` Here 's a lovely flock of lamb all lie down , '' say Amy .
`` See , Papa , be n't they pretty ? ''
add Flo sentimentally .
`` Geese , young lady , '' return Uncle , in a tone that keep u quiet till Flo settle down to enjoy the Flirtations of Captain Cavendish , and I have the scenery all to myself .
Of course it rain when we get to London , and there be nothing to be see but fog and umbrella .
We rest , unpacked , and shop a little between the shower .
Aunt Mary get me some new thing , for I come off in such a hurry I be n't half ready .
A white hat and blue feather , a muslin dress to match , and the lovely mantle you ever saw .
Shopping in Regent Street be perfectly splendid .
Things seem so cheap , nice ribbon only sixpence a yard .
I lay in a stock , but shall get my glove in Paris .
Does n't that sound sort of elegant and rich ?
Flo and I , for the fun of it , order a hansom cab , while Aunt and Uncle be out , and go for a drive , though we learn afterward that it be n't the thing for young lady to ride in them alone .
It be so droll !
For when we be shut in by the wooden apron , the man drive so fast that Flo be frighten , and tell me to stop him , but he be up outside behind somewhere , and I could n't get at him .
He do n't hear me call , nor see me flap my parasol in front , and there we be , quite helpless , rattle away , and whirl around corner at a breakneck pace .
At last , in my despair , I saw a little door in the roof , and on poke it open , a red eye appear , and a beery voice say ... `` Now , then , mum ? ''

I poke again and say , `` A little faster , '' then off he go , helter-skelter a before , and we resign ourselves to our fate .
Today be fair , and we go to Hyde Park , close by , for we be more aristocratic than we look .
The Duke of Devonshire live near .
I often see his footman lounge at the back gate , and the Duke of Wellington 's house be not far off .
Such sight a I saw , my dear !

Smart maid , with the rosy child I ever saw , handsome girl , look half asleep , dandy in queer English hat and lavender kid lounge about , and tall soldier , in short red jacket and muffin cap stick on one side , look so funny I long to sketch them .
Rotten Row mean ` Route de Roi ' , or the king 's way , but now it 's more like a rid school than anything else .
The horse be splendid , and the men , especially the groom , ride well , but the woman be stiff , and bounce , which be n't accord to our rule .
I long to show them a tearing American gallop , for they trot solemnly up and down , in their scant habit and high hat , look like the woman in a toy Noah 's Ark . .
Everyone ride -- old men , stout lady , little child -- and the young folk do a deal of flirt here , I saw a pair exchange rise bud , for it 's the thing to wear one in the button-hole , and I think it rather a nice little idea .

That be so Frenchy .

Adieu , I embrace you tenderly .

You know Mrs. Kirke write to you for some respectable young person to teach her child and sew .
It 's rather hard to find just the thing , but I think I should suit if I try . ''
`` My dear , go out to service in that great boarding house ! ''
and Mrs. March look surprised , but not displeased .
`` It 's not exactly go out to service , for Mrs. Kirke be your friend -- the kind soul that ever live -- and would make thing pleasant for me , I know .
Her family be separate from the rest , and no one know me there .
Do n't care if they do .
It 's honest work , and I 'm not ashamed of it . ''
`` Nor I .
But your writing ? ''
`` All the good for the change .
I shall see and hear new thing , get new idea , and even if I have n't much time there , I shall bring home quantity of material for my rubbish . ''
`` I have no doubt of it , but be these your only reason for this sudden fancy ? ''
`` No , Mother . ''
`` May I know the others ? ''
Jo look up and Jo look down , then say slowly , with sudden color in her cheek .
`` It may be vain and wrong to say it , but -- I 'm afraid -- Laurie be get too fond of me . ''
`` Then you do n't care for him in the way it be evident he begin to care for you ? ''
and Mrs. March look anxious a she put the question .
`` Mercy , no !
I love the dear boy , a I always have , and be immensely proud of him , but a for anything more , it 's out of the question . ''
`` I 'm glad of that , Jo . ''
`` Why , please ? ''
`` Because , dear , I do n't think you suit to one another .
As friend you be very happy , and your frequent quarrel soon blow over , but I fear you would both rebel if you be mat for life .
You be too much alike and too fond of freedom , not to mention hot temper and strong will , to get on happily together , in a relation which need infinite patience and forbearance , as well a love . ''
`` That 's just the feeling I have , though I could n't express it .
I 'm glad you think he be only begin to care for me .
It would trouble me sadly to make him unhappy , for I could n't fall in love with the dear old fellow merely out of gratitude , could I ? ''
`` You be sure of his feeling for you ? ''
The color deepen in Jo 's cheek a she answer , with the look of mingled pleasure , pride , and pain which young girl wear when speaking of first lover , `` I 'm afraid it be so , Mother .
He have n't say anything , but he look a great deal .
I think I have well go away before it come to anything . ''
`` I agree with you , and if it can be manage you shall go . ''
Jo look relieve , and after a pause , say , smile , `` How Mrs. Moffat would wonder at your want of management , if she know , and how she will rejoice that Annie may still hope . ''
`` Ah , Jo , mother may differ in their management , but the hope be the same in all -- the desire to see their child happy .
Meg be so , and I be content with her success .
You I leave to enjoy your liberty till you tire of it , for only then will you find that there be something sweeter .
Amy be my chief care now , but her good sense will help her .
For Beth , I indulge no hope except that she may be well .
By the way , she seem brighter this last day or two .
Have you speak to her ? '
`` Yes , she own she have a trouble , and promise to tell me by-and-by .
I say no more , for I think I know it , '' and Jo tell her little story .
Mrs. March shake her head , and do not take so romantic a view of the case , but look grave , and repeat her opinion that for Laurie 's sake Jo should go away for a time .
`` Let u say nothing about it to him till the plan be settle , then I 'll run away before he can collect his wit and be tragic .
Beth must think I 'm go to please myself , a I be , for I ca n't talk about Laurie to her .
But she can pet and comfort him after I 'm go , and so cure him of this romantic notion .
He 's be through so many little trial of the sort , he 's use to it , and will soon get over his lovelornity . ''
Jo speak hopefully , but could not rid herself of the forebode fear that this ` little trial ' would be hard than the others , and that Laurie would not get over his ` lovelornity ' as easily a heretofore .
The plan be talk over in a family council and agree upon , for Mrs. Kirke gladly accept Jo , and promise to make a pleasant home for her .
The teaching would render her independent , and such leisure a she get might be make profitable by write , while the new scene and society would be both useful and agreeable .
Jo like the prospect and be eager to be go , for the home nest be grow too narrow for her restless nature and adventurous spirit .
When all be settle , with fear and tremble she tell Laurie , but to her surprise he take it very quietly .
He have be graver than usual of late , but very pleasant , and when jokingly accuse of turn over a new leaf , he answer soberly , `` So I be , and I mean this one shall stay turned . ''
Jo be very much relieve that one of his virtuous fit should come on just then , and make her preparation with a lightened heart , for Beth seem more cheerful , and hop she be do the best for all .
`` One thing I leave in your especial care , '' she say , the night before she leave .
`` You mean your paper ? ''
ask Beth .
`` No , my boy .
Be very good to him , wo n't you ? ''
`` Of course I will , but I ca n't fill your place , and he 'll miss you sadly . ''
`` It wo n't hurt him , so remember , I leave him in your charge , to plague , pet , and keep in order . ''
`` I 'll do my best , for your sake , '' promise Beth , wonder why Jo look at her so queerly .

My eye be on you , so mind what you do , or I 'll come and bring you home . ''
CHAPTER THIRTY-THREE JO 'S JOURNAL New York , November Dear Marmee and Beth , I 'm go to write you a regular volume , for I 've get heap to tell , though I 'm not a fine young lady travel on the continent .
When I lose sight of Father 's dear old face , I felt a trifle blue , and might have shed a briny drop or two , if an Irish lady with four small child , all cry more or less , have n't divert my mind , for I amuse myself by drop gingerbread nut over the seat every time they open their mouth to roar .
Soon the sun come out , and take it a a good omen , I clear up likewise and enjoy my journey with all my heart .
Mrs. Kirke welcome me so kindly I felt at home at once , even in that big house full of stranger .
She give me a funny little sky parlor -- all she have , but there be a stove in it , and a nice table in a sunny window , so I can sit here and write whenever I like .
A fine view and a church tower opposite atone for the many stair , and I take a fancy to my den on the spot .
The nursery , where I be to teach and sew , be a pleasant room next Mrs. Kirke 's private parlor , and the two little girl be pretty child , rather spoil , I fancy , but they take to me after tell them The Seven Bad Pigs , and I 've no doubt I shall make a model governess .
I be to have my meal with the child , if I prefer it to the great table , and for the present I do , for I be bashful , though no one will believe it .
`` Now , my dear , make yourself at home , '' say Mrs. K. in her motherly way , `` I 'm on the drive from morning to night , a you may suppose with such a family , but a great anxiety will be off my mind if I know the child be safe with you .
My room be always open to you , and your own shall be as comfortable a I can make it .
There be some pleasant people in the house if you feel sociable , and your evening be always free .
Come to me if anything go wrong , and be as happy a you can .
There 's the tea bell , I must run and change my cap . ''
And off she bustle , leave me to settle myself in my new nest .
As I go downstairs soon after , I saw something I like .
The flight be very long in this tall house , and a I stand wait at the head of the third one for a little servant girl to lumber up , I saw a gentleman come along behind her , take the heavy hod of coal out of her hand , carry it all the way up , put it down at a door near by , and walk away , say , with a kind nod and a foreign accent , `` It go well so .
The little back be too young to haf such heaviness . ''
Was n't it good of him ?
I like such thing , for a Father say , trifle show character .
When I mention it to Mrs. K. , that evening , she laugh , and say , `` That must have be Professor Bhaer , he 's always do thing of that sort . ''
Mrs. K. tell me he be from Berlin , very learned and good , but poor a a church mouse , and give lesson to support himself and two little orphan nephew whom he be educate here , accord to the wish of his sister , who marry an American .
Not a very romantic story , but it interest me , and I be glad to hear that Mrs. K. lend him her parlor for some of his scholar .
There be a glass door between it and the nursery , and I mean to peep at him , and then I 'll tell you how he look .
He 's almost forty , so it 's no harm , Marmee .
After tea and a go-to-bed romp with the little girl , I attack the big workbasket , and have a quiet evening chat with my new friend .
I shall keep a journal-letter , and send it once a week , so goodnight , and more tomorrow .
Tuesday Eve Had a lively time in my seminary this morning , for the child act like Sancho , and at one time I really think I should shake them all round .
Some good angel inspire me to try gymnastics , and I keep it up till they be glad to sit down and keep still .
After luncheon , the girl take them out for a walk , and I go to my needlework like little Mabel ` with a willing mind ' .
I be thank my star that I 'd learn to make nice buttonhole , when the parlor door open and shut , and someone begin to hum , Kennst Du Das Land , like a big bumblebee .
It be dreadfully improper , I know , but I could n't resist the temptation , and lift one end of the curtain before the glass door , I peep in .
Professor Bhaer be there , and while he arrange his book , I take a good look at him .
A regular German -- rather stout , with brown hair tumble all over his head , a bushy beard , good nose , the kind eye I ever saw , and a splendid big voice that do one 's ear good , after our sharp or slipshod American gabble .
His clothes be rusty , his hand be large , and he have n't a really handsome feature in his face , except his beautiful teeth , yet I like him , for he have a fine head , his linen be very nice , and he look like a gentleman , though two button be off his coat and there be a patch on one shoe .
He look sober in spite of his humming , till he go to the window to turn the hyacinth bulbs toward the sun , and stroke the cat , who receive him like an old friend .
Then he smile , and when a tap come at the door , call out in a loud , brisk tone , `` Herein ! ''
I be just go to run , when I catch sight of a morsel of a child carry a big book , and stop , to see what be go on .
`` Me want me Bhaer , '' say the mite , slam down her book and run to meet him .
`` Thou shalt haf thy Bhaer .
Come , then , and take a goot hug from him , my Tina , '' say the Professor , catch her up with a laugh , and hold her so high over his head that she have to stoop her little face to kiss him .
`` Now me mus tuddy my lessin , '' go on the funny little thing .
So he put her up at the table , open the great dictionary she have bring , and give her a paper and pencil , and she scribble away , turn a leaf now and then , and pass her little fat finger down the page , a if find a word , so soberly that I nearly betray myself by a laugh , while Mr. Bhaer stand stroke her pretty hair with a fatherly look that make me think she must be his own , though she look more French than German .
Another knock and the appearance of two young lady send me back to my work , and there I virtuously remain through all the noise and gabbling that go on next door .
One of the girl keep laugh affectedly , and say , `` Now Professor , '' in a coquettish tone , and the other pronounce her German with an accent that must have make it hard for him to keep sober .
Both seem to try his patience sorely , for more than once I hear him say emphatically , `` No , no , it be not so , you haf not attend to what I say , '' and once there be a loud rap , a if he strike the table with his book , follow by the despairing exclamation , `` Prut !
It all go bad this day . ''
Poor man , I pity him , and when the girl be go , take just one more peep to see if he survive it .
He seem to have throw himself back in his chair , tire out , and sit there with his eye shut till the clock strike two , when he jump up , put his book in his pocket , a if ready for another lesson , and take little Tina who have fall asleep on the sofa in his arm , he carry her quietly away .
I fancy he have a hard life of it .
Mrs. Kirke ask me if I would n't go down to the five o'clock dinner , and feel a little bit homesick , I think I would , just to see what sort of people be under the same roof with me .
So I make myself respectable and try to slip in behind Mrs. Kirke , but a she be short and I 'm tall , my effort at concealment be rather a failure .
She give me a seat by her , and after my face cool off , I pluck up courage and look about me .
The long table be full , and every one intent on get their dinner , the gentleman especially , who seem to be eat on time , for they bolt in every sense of the word , vanish as soon a they be do .
There be the usual assortment of young men absorb in themselves , young couple absorb in each other , married lady in their baby , and old gentleman in politics .

`` Governess , or something of that sort . ''
`` What the deuce be she at our table for ? ''

`` Handsome head , but no style . ''
`` Not a bit of it .
Give u a light and come on . ''

Thursday Yesterday be a quiet day spend in teaching , sewing , and write in my little room , which be very cozy , with a light and fire .
I pick up a few bit of news and be introduce to the Professor .

P.S . On reading over my letter , it strike me a rather Bhaery , but I be always interested in odd people , and I really have nothing else to write about .

DECEMBER My Precious Betsey , As this be to be a scribble-scrabble letter , I direct it to you , for it may amuse you , and give you some idea of my going on , for though quiet , they be rather amusing , for which , oh , be joyful !
After what Amy would call Herculaneum effort , in the way of mental and moral agriculture , my young idea begin to shoot and my little twig to bend a I could wish .
They be not so interesting to me a Tina and the boy , but I do my duty by them , and they be fond of me .
Franz and Emil be jolly little lad , quite after my own heart , for the mixture of German and American spirit in them produce a constant state of effervescence .
Saturday afternoon be riotous time , whether spend in the house or out , for on pleasant day they all go to walk , like a seminary , with the Professor and myself to keep order , and then such fun !
We be very good friend now , and I 've begin to take lesson .
I really could n't help it , and it all come about in such a droll way that I must tell you .
To begin at the beginning , Mrs. Kirke call to me one day a I pass Mr. Bhaer 's room where she be rummage .

he say , a I stop and star like a goose , `` you peep at me , I peep at you , and this be not bad , but see , I be not pleasanting when I say , haf you a wish for German ? ''

We will make the time , and we fail not to find the sense .

I take four lesson , and then I stick fast in a grammatical bog .
The Professor be very patient with me , but it must have be torment to him , and now and then he 'd look at me with such an expression of mild despair that it be a toss-up with me whether to laugh or cry .

I felt myself disgrace and desert forever , but do n't blame him a particle , and be scramble my paper together , mean to rush upstairs and shake myself hard , when in he come , a brisk and beaming a if I 'd cover myself in glory .
`` Now we shall try a new way .

He speak so kindly , and open Hans Anderson 's fairy tale so invitingly before me , that I be more ashamed than ever , and go at my lesson in a neck-or-nothing style that seem to amuse him immensely .
I forget my bashfulness , and peg away -LRB- no other word will express it -RRB- with all my might , tumble over long word , pronounce accord to inspiration of the minute , and do my very best .
When I finish read my first page , and stop for breath , he clap his hand and cry out in his hearty way , `` Das ist gut !
Now we go well !
My turn .
I do him in German , gif me your ear . ''
And away he go , rumble out the word with his strong voice and a relish which be good to see as well a hear .

After that we get on good , and now I read my lesson pretty well , for this way of study suit me , and I can see that the grammar get tuck into the tale and poetry a one give pill in jelly .
I like it very much , and he do n't seem tire of it yet , which be very good of him , be n't it ?
I mean to give him something on Christmas , for I dare not offer money .
Tell me something nice , Marmee .

I 'm afraid I could n't like him without a spice of human naughtiness .

I have n't time to write much , and that will do just as well .
Thank Heaven Beth continue so comfortable .
JANUARY A Happy New Year to you all , my dear family , which of course include Mr. L. and a young man by the name of Teddy .
I ca n't tell you how much I enjoy your Christmas bundle , for I do n't get it till night and have give up hop .
Your letter come in the morning , but you say nothing about a parcel , mean it for a surprise , so I be disappoint , for I 'd have a ` kind of feel ' that you would n't forget me .
I felt a little low in my mind a I sit up in my room after tea , and when the big , muddy , battered-looking bundle be bring to me , I just hug it and prance .
It be so homey and refresh that I sit down on the floor and read and look and ate and laugh and cry , in my usual absurd way .
The thing be just what I want , and all the good for be make instead of bought .
Beth 's new ` ink bib ' be capital , and Hannah 's box of hard gingerbread will be a treasure .
I 'll be sure and wear the nice flannel you send , Marmee , and read carefully the book Father have mark .
Thank you all , heap and heap !
Speaking of book reminds me that I 'm get rich in that line , for on New Year 's Day Mr. Bhaer give me a fine Shakespeare .
It be one he value much , and I 've often admire it , set up in the place of honor with his German Bible , Plato , Homer , and Milton , so you may imagine how I felt when he bring it down , without it cover , and show me my own name in it , `` from my friend Friedrich Bhaer '' .
`` You say often you wish a library .
Here I gif you one , for between these lid -LRB- he mean cover -RRB- be many book in one .
Read him well , and he will help you much , for the study of character in this book will help you to read it in the world and paint it with your pen . ''
I thank him as well a I could , and talk now about ` my library ' , a if I have a hundred book .
I never know how much there be in Shakespeare before , but then I never have a Bhaer to explain it to me .
Now do n't laugh at his horrid name .
It be n't pronounce either Bear or Beer , a people will say it , but something between the two , a only Germans can give it .
I 'm glad you both like what I tell you about him , and hope you will know him some day .
Mother would admire his warm heart , Father his wise head .
I admire both , and feel rich in my new ` friend Friedrich Bhaer ' .
Not have much money , or know what he 'd like , I get several little thing , and put them about the room , where he would find them unexpectedly .
They be useful , pretty , or funny , a new standish on his table , a little vase for his flower , he always have one , or a bit of green in a glass , to keep him fresh , he say , and a holder for his blower , so that he need n't burn up what Amy call ` mouchoirs ' .
I make it like those Beth invent , a big butterfly with a fat body , and black and yellow wing , worst feeler , and bead eye .
It take his fancy immensely , and he put it on his mantlepiece a an article of virtue , so it be rather a failure after all .
Poor a he be , he do n't forget a servant or a child in the house , and not a soul here , from the French laundrywoman to Miss Norton forget him .

CHAPTER THIRTY-SIX BETH 'S SECRET When Jo come home that spring , she have be strike with the change in Beth .

It be no paler and but little thinner than in the autumn , yet there be a strange , transparent look about it , a if the mortal be be slowly refine away , and the immortal shining through the frail flesh with an indescribably pathetic beauty .
Jo saw and felt it , but say nothing at the time , and soon the first impression lose much of it power , for Beth seem happy , no one appear to doubt that she be well , and presently in other care Jo for a time forget her fear .
But when Laurie be go , and peace prevail again , the vague anxiety return and haunt her .
She have confess her sin and be forgiven , but when she show her saving and propose a mountain trip , Beth have thank her heartily , but beg not to go so far away from home .
Another little visit to the seashore would suit her good , and a Grandma could not be prevail upon to leave the baby , Jo take Beth down to the quiet place , where she could live much in the open air , and let the fresh sea breeze blow a little color into her pale cheek .
It be not a fashionable place , but even among the pleasant people there , the girl make few friend , prefer to live for one another .
Beth be too shy to enjoy society , and Jo too wrap up in her to care for anyone else .
So they be all in all to each other , and come and go , quite unconscious of the interest they exit in those about them , who watch with sympathetic eye the strong sister and the feeble one , always together , a if they felt instinctively that a long separation be not far away .
They do feel it , yet neither spoke of it , for often between ourselves and those near and dear to u there exist a reserve which it be very hard to overcome .
Jo felt a if a veil have fall between her heart and Beth 's , but when she put out her hand to lift it up , there seem something sacred in the silence , and she wait for Beth to speak .
She wonder , and be thankful also , that her parent do not seem to see what she saw , and during the quiet week when the shadow grow so plain to her , she say nothing of it to those at home , believe that it would tell itself when Beth come back no good .
She wonder still more if her sister really guess the hard truth , and what thought be pass through her mind during the long hour when she lay on the warm rock with her head in Jo 's lap , while the wind blow healthfully over her and the sea make music at her foot .
One day Beth tell her .

Simple , sincere people seldom speak much of their piety .
It show itself in act rather than in word , and have more influence than homily or protestation .
Beth could not reason upon or explain the faith that give her courage and patience to give up life , and cheerfully wait for death .
Like a confiding child , she ask no question , but leave everything to God and nature , Father and Mother of u all , feel sure that they , and they only , could teach and strengthen heart and spirit for this life and the life to come .
She do not rebuke Jo with saintly speech , only love her good for her passionate affection , and clung more closely to the dear human love , from which our Father never mean u to be wean , but through which He draw u close to Himself .

CHAPTER THIRTY-EIGHT ON THE SHELF In France the young girl have a dull time of it till they be marry , when ` Vive la liberte ! '
becomes their motto .
In America , a everyone know , girl early sign the declaration of independence , and enjoy their freedom with republican zest , but the young matron usually abdicate with the first heir to the throne and go into a seclusion almost as close a a French nunnery , though by no mean a quiet .

As she be a womanly little woman , the maternal instinct be very strong , and she be entirely absorb in her child , to the utter exclusion of everything and everybody else .

But three month pass , and there be no return of repose .
Meg look worn and nervous , the baby absorb every minute of her time , the house be neglect , and Kitty , the cook , who take life ` aisy ' , keep him on short common .
When he go out in the morning he be bewilder by small commission for the captive mamma , if he come gaily in at night , eager to embrace his family , he be quench by a `` Hush !
They be just asleep after worry all day . ''
If he propose a little amusement at home , `` No , it would disturb the baby . ''
If he hint at a lecture or a concert , he be answer with a reproachful look , and a decided -- `` Leave my child for pleasure , never ! ''
His sleep be break by infant wail and vision of a phantom figure pace noiselessly to and fro in the watch of the night .
His meal be interrupt by the frequent flight of the preside genius , who desert him , half-helped , if a muffled chirp sound from the nest above .
And when he read his paper of an evening , Demi 's colic get into the shipping list and Daisy 's fall affect the price of stock , for Mrs. Brooke be only interested in domestic news .
The poor man be very uncomfortable , for the child have bereft him of his wife , home be merely a nursery and the perpetual ` hush ' make him feel like a brutal intruder whenever he enter the sacred precinct of Babyland .
He bore it very patiently for six month , and when no sign of amendment appear , he do what other paternal exile do -- try to get a little comfort elsewhere .
Scott have marry and go to housekeep not far off , and John fell into the way of run over for an hour or two of an evening , when his own parlor be empty , and his own wife sing lullaby that seem to have no end .
Mrs. Scott be a lively , pretty girl , with nothing to do but be agreeable , and she perform her mission most successfully .
The parlor be always bright and attractive , the chessboard ready , the piano in tune , plenty of gay gossip , and a nice little supper set forth in tempt style .
John would have prefer his own fireside if it have not be so lonely , but a it be he gratefully take the next best thing and enjoy his neighbor 's society .
Meg rather approve of the new arrangement at first , and find it a relief to know that John be have a good time instead of doze in the parlor , or tramp about the house and wake the child .
But by-and-by , when the teething worry be over and the idol go to sleep at proper hour , leave Mamma time to rest , she begin to miss John , and find her workbasket dull company , when he be not sit opposite in his old dressing gown , comfortably scorch his slipper on the fender .
She would not ask him to stay at home , but felt injured because he do not know that she want him without be tell , entirely forget the many evening he have wait for her in vain .
She be nervous and wear out with watch and worry , and in that unreasonable frame of mind which the best of mother occasionally experience when domestic care oppress them .
Want of exercise rob them of cheerfulness , and too much devotion to that idol of American woman , the teapot , make them feel a if they be all nerve and no muscle .
`` Yes , '' she would say , look in the glass , `` I 'm get old and ugly .
John do n't find me interest any long , so he leave his faded wife and go to see his pretty neighbor , who have no incumbrance .
Well , the baby love me , they do n't care if I be thin and pale and have n't time to crimp my hair , they be my comfort , and some day John will see what I 've gladly sacrifice for them , wo n't he , my precious ? ''
To which pathetic appeal Daisy would answer with a coo , or Demi with a crow , and Meg would put by her lamentation for a maternal revel , which soothe her solitude for the time be .
But the pain increase a politics absorbed John , who be always run over to discuss interesting point with Scott , quite unconscious that Meg miss him .
Not a word do she say , however , till her mother find her in tears one day , and insist on know what the matter be , for Meg 's droop spirit have not escape her observation .
`` I would n't tell anyone except you , Mother , but I really do need advice , for if John go on much long I might as well be widow , '' reply Mrs. Brooke , dry her tear on Daisy 's bib with an injured air .
`` Goes on how , my dear ? ''
ask her mother anxiously .
`` He 's away all day , and at night when I want to see him , he be continually go over to the Scotts ' .
It be n't fair that I should have the hard work , and never any amusement .
Men be very selfish , even the best of them . ''
`` So be woman .
Do n't blame John till you see where you be wrong yourself . ''
`` But it ca n't be right for him to neglect me . ''
`` Do n't you neglect him ? ''
`` Why , Mother , I think you 'd take my part ! ''
`` So I do , as far a sympathizing go , but I think the fault be yours , Meg . ''
`` I do n't see how . ''
`` Let me show you .
Did John ever neglect you , a you call it , while you make it a point to give him your society of an evening , his only leisure time ? ''

`` I think you could , dear , and I think you ought .
May I speak quite freely , and will you remember that it 's Mother who blame as well a Mother who sympathize ? ''

Speak to me a if I be little Meg again .

That be the secret of our home happiness .
He do not let business wean him from the little care and duty that affect u all , and I try not to let domestic worry destroy my interest in his pursuit .
Each do our part alone in many thing , but at home we work together , always . ''

Show me how , I 'll do anything you say . ''

Then I 'd do what I have often propose , let Hannah come and help you .
She be a capital nurse , and you may trust the precious baby to her while you do more housework .

Love cover a multitude of sin , and of whom could you ask more freely than of him ?
Try it , and see if he do n't find your society far more agreeable than Mrs. Scott 's supper . ''

Poor John !

So Master Demi early discover that when he undertake to ` wrastle ' with ` Parpar ' , he always get the bad of it , yet like the Englishman , baby respect the man who conquer him , and love the father whose grave `` No , no , '' be more impressive than all Mamma 's love pat .

Will you , lovey ? ''
`` Iss ! ''
and Demi shut his eye tight , a if to catch sleep and hurry the desired day .

This taste right .

John saw in a minute that a revolution of some kind be go on , but wisely ask no question , know that Meg be such a transparent little person , she could n't keep a secret to save her life , and therefore the clue would soon appear .
He read a long debate with the most amiable readiness and then explain it in his most lucid manner , while Meg try to look deeply interested , to ask intelligent question , and keep her thought from wander from the state of the nation to the state of her bonnet .
In her secret soul , however , she decide that politics be as bad a mathematics , and that the mission of politician seem to be call each other name , but she keep these feminine idea to herself , and when John pause , shake her head and say with what she think diplomatic ambiguity , `` Well , I really do n't see what we be come to . ''
John laugh , and watch her for a minute , a she poise a pretty little preparation of lace and flower on her hand , and regard it with the genuine interest which his harangue have fail to waken .
`` She be try to like politics for my sake , so I 'll try and like millinery for hers , that 's only fair , '' think John the Just , add aloud , `` That 's very pretty .
Is it what you call a breakfast cap ? ''

My very best go-to-concert-and-theater bonnet . ''

`` It 's a love of a bonnet , but I prefer the face inside , for it look young and happy again , '' and John kiss the smile face , to the great detriment of the rosebud under the chin .
`` I 'm glad you like it , for I want you to take me to one of the new concert some night .
I really need some music to put me in tune .
Will you , please ? ''
`` Of course I will , with all my heart , or anywhere else you like .
You have be shut up so long , it will do you no end of good , and I shall enjoy it , of all thing .
What put it into your head , little mother ? ''
`` Well , I have a talk with Marmee the other day , and tell her how nervous and cross and out of sort I felt , and she say I need change and less care , so Hannah be to help me with the child , and I 'm to see to thing about the house more , and now and then have a little fun , just to keep me from get to be a fidgety , broken-down old woman before my time .
It 's only an experiment , John , and I want to try it for your sake as much a for mine , because I 've neglect you shamefully lately , and I 'm go to make home what it use to be , if I can .

Never mind what John say , or what a very narrow escape the little bonnet have from utter ruin .
All that we have any business to know be that John do not appear to object , judge from the change which gradually take place in the house and it inmate .
It be not all Paradise by any mean , but everyone be well for the division of labor system .
The child thrive under the paternal rule , for accurate , steadfast John bring order and obedience into Babydom , while Meg recover her spirit and compose her nerve by plenty of wholesome exercise , a little pleasure , and much confidential conversation with her sensible husband .
Home grow homelike again , and John have no wish to leave it , unless he take Meg with him .
The Scotts come to the Brookes ' now , and everyone find the little house a cheerful place , full of happiness , content , and family love .
Even Sallie Moffatt like to go there .
`` It be always so quiet and pleasant here , it do me good , Meg , '' she use to say , look about her with wistful eye , a if try to discover the charm , that she might use it in her great house , full of splendid loneliness , for there be no riotous , sunny-faced baby there , and Ned live in a world of his own , where there be no place for her .
This household happiness do not come all at once , but John and Meg have find the key to it , and each year of married life teach them how to use it , unlock the treasury of real home love and mutual helpfulness , which the poor may possess , and the rich can not buy .
This be the sort of shelf on which young wife and mother may consent to be lay , safe from the restless fret and fever of the world , find loyal lover in the little son and daughter who cling to them , undaunted by sorrow , poverty , or age , walk side by side , through fair and stormy weather , with a faithful friend , who be , in the true sense of the good old Saxon word , the ` house-band ' , and learning , a Meg learn , that a woman 's happy kingdom be home , her high honor the art of rule it not a a queen , but a a wise wife and mother .
CHAPTER THIRTY-NINE LAZY LAURENCE Laurie go to Nice intend to stay a week , and remain a month .
He be tire of wander about alone , and Amy 's familiar presence seem to give a homelike charm to the foreign scene in which she bore a part .
He rather miss the ` petting ' he use to receive , and enjoy a taste of it again , for no attention , however flatter , from stranger , be half so pleasant a the sisterly adoration of the girl at home .
Amy never would pet him like the others , but she be very glad to see him now , and quite clung to him , feel that he be the representative of the dear family for whom she long more than she would confess .
They naturally take comfort in each other 's society and be much together , rid , walk , dance , or dawdling , for at Nice no one can be very industrious during the gay season .
But , while apparently amuse themselves in the most careless fashion , they be half-consciously make discovery and form opinion about each other .
Amy rise daily in the estimation of her friend , but he sink in hers , and each felt the truth before a word be speak .
Amy try to please , and succeed , for she be grateful for the many pleasure he give her , and repay him with the little service to which womanly woman know how to lend an indescribable charm .
Laurie make no effort of any kind , but just let himself drift along as comfortably a possible , try to forget , and feel that all woman owe him a kind word because one have be cold to him .
It cost him no effort to be generous , and he would have give Amy all the trinket in Nice if she would have take them , but at the same time he felt that he could not change the opinion she be form of him , and he rather dread the keen blue eye that seem to watch him with such half-sorrowful , half-scornful surprise .
`` All the rest have go to Monaco for the day .
I prefer to stay at home and write letter .
They be do now , and I be go to Valrosa to sketch , will you come ? ''
say Amy , a she join Laurie one lovely day when he lounge in a usual , about noon .
`` Well , yes , but be n't it rather warm for such a long walk ? ''
he answer slowly , for the shaded salon look inviting after the glare without .
`` I 'm go to have the little carriage , and Baptiste can drive , so you 'll have nothing to do but hold your umbrella , and keep your glove nice , '' return Amy , with a sarcastic glance at the immaculate kid , which be a weak point with Laurie .
`` Then I 'll go with pleasure . ''
and he put out his hand for her sketchbook .
But she tuck it under her arm with a sharp ... `` Do n't trouble yourself .
It 's no exertion to me , but you do n't look equal to it . ''
Laurie lift his eyebrow and follow at a leisurely pace a she run downstairs , but when they get into the carriage he take the rein himself , and leave little Baptiste nothing to do but fold his arm and fall asleep on his perch .
The two never quarrel .
Amy be too well-bred , and just now Laurie be too lazy , so in a minute he peep under her hatbrim with an inquire air .
She answer him with a smile , and they go on together in the most amicable manner .
It be a lovely drive , along wind road rich in the picturesque scenes that delight beauty-loving eye .
Here an ancient monastery , whence the solemn chanting of the monk come down to them .
There a bare-legged shepherd , in wooden shoe , point hat , and rough jacket over one shoulder , sit pip on a stone while his goat skip among the rock or lay at his foot .
Meek , mouse-colored donkey , laden with pannier of freshly cut grass pass by , with a pretty girl in a capaline sit between the green pile , or an old woman spin with a distaff a she go .
Brown , soft-eyed child run out from the quaint stone hovel to offer nosegay , or bunch of orange still on the bough .
Gnarled olive tree cover the hill with their dusky foliage , fruit hung golden in the orchard , and great scarlet anemone fringe the roadside , while beyond green slope and craggy height , the Maritime Alps rise sharp and white against the blue Italian sky .
Valrosa well deserve it name , for in that climate of perpetual summer rose blossom everywhere .
They overhang the archway , thrust themselves between the bar of the great gate with a sweet welcome to passers-by , and line the avenue , wind through lemon tree and feathery palm up to the villa on the hill .
Every shadowy nook , where seat invite one to stop and rest , be a mass of bloom , every cool grotto have it marble nymph smile from a veil of flower and every fountain reflect crimson , white , or pale pink rose , lean down to smile at their own beauty .
Roses cover the wall of the house , drape the cornice , climb the pillar , and run riot over the balustrade of the wide terrace , whence one look down on the sunny Mediterranean , and the white-walled city on it shore .
`` This be a regular honeymoon paradise , be n't it ?
Did you ever see such rose ? ''
ask Amy , pause on the terrace to enjoy the view , and a luxurious whiff of perfume that come wander by .
`` No , nor felt such thorn , '' return Laurie , with his thumb in his mouth , after a vain attempt to capture a solitary scarlet flower that grow just beyond his reach .
`` Try low down , and pick those that have no thorn , '' say Amy , gather three of the tiny cream-colored one that star the wall behind her .
She put them in his buttonhole a a peace offering , and he stand a minute look down at them with a curious expression , for in the Italian part of his nature there be a touch of superstition , and he be just then in that state of half-sweet , half-bitter melancholy , when imaginative young men find significance in trifle and food for romance everywhere .
He have think of Jo in reach after the thorny red rise , for vivid flower become her , and she have often worn one like that from the greenhouse at home .
The pale rose Amy give him be the sort that the Italians lay in dead hand , never in bridal wreath , and for a moment he wonder if the omen be for Jo or for himself , but the next instant his American common sense get the good of sentimentality , and he laugh a hearty laugh than Amy have hear since he come .
`` It 's good advice , you 'd better take it and save your finger , '' she say , think her speech amuse him .
`` Thank you , I will , '' he answer in jest , and a few month later he do it in earnest .
`` Laurie , when be you go to your grandfather ? ''
she ask presently , a she settle herself on a rustic seat .
`` Very soon . ''
`` You have say that a dozen time within the last three week . ''
`` I dare say , short answer save trouble . ''
`` He expect you , and you really ought to go . ''
`` Hospitable creature !
I know it . ''
`` Then why do n't you do it ? ''
`` Natural depravity , I suppose . ''
`` Natural indolence , you mean .
It 's really dreadful ! ''
and Amy look severe .
`` Not so bad a it seem , for I should only plague him if I go , so I might as well stay and plague you a little long , you can bear it good , in fact I think it agree with you excellently , '' and Laurie compose himself for a lounge on the broad ledge of the balustrade .
Amy shake her head and open her sketchbook with an air of resignation , but she have make up her mind to lecture ` that boy ' and in a minute she begin again .
`` What be you do just now ? ''
`` Watching lizard . ''
`` No , no .
I mean what do you intend and wish to do ? ''
`` Smoke a cigarette , if you 'll allow me . ''
`` How provoking you be !
I do n't approve of cigar and I will only allow it on condition that you let me put you into my sketch .
I need a figure . ''
`` With all the pleasure in life .
How will you have me , full length or three-quarters , on my head or my heel ?
I should respectfully suggest a recumbent posture , then put yourself in also and call it ` Dolce far niente ' . ''
`` Stay a you be , and go to sleep if you like .
I intend to work hard , '' say Amy in her most energetic tone .
`` What delightful enthusiasm ! ''
and he lean against a tall urn with an air of entire satisfaction .
`` What would Jo say if she saw you now ? ''
ask Amy impatiently , hop to stir him up by the mention of her still more energetic sister 's name .
`` As usual , ` Go away , Teddy .
I 'm busy ! ' ''
He laugh a he speak , but the laugh be not natural , and a shade pass over his face , for the utterance of the familiar name touch the wound that be not heal yet .
Both tone and shadow struck Amy , for she have see and hear them before , and now she look up in time to catch a new expression on Laurie 's face -- a hard bitter look , full of pain , dissatisfaction , and regret .
It be go before she could study it and the listless expression back again .
She watch him for a moment with artistic pleasure , think how like an Italian he look , a he lay bask in the sun with uncovered head and eye full of southern dreaminess , for he seem to have forget her and fall into a reverie .
`` You look like the effigy of a young knight asleep on his tomb , '' she say , carefully trace the well-cut profile define against the dark stone .
`` Wish I be ! ''
`` That 's a foolish wish , unless you have spoil your life .
You be so changed , I sometimes think -- '' there Amy stop , with a half-timid , half-wistful look , more significant than her unfinished speech .
Laurie saw and understand the affectionate anxiety which she hesitate to express , and look straight into her eye , say , just a he use to say it to her mother , `` It 's all right , ma'am . ''

CHAPTER FORTY THE VALLEY OF THE SHADOW When the first bitterness be over , the family accept the inevitable , and try to bear it cheerfully , help one another by the increase affection which come to bind household tenderly together in time of trouble .
They put away their grief , and each do his or her part toward make that last year a happy one .
The pleasant room in the house be set apart for Beth , and in it be gather everything that she most love , flower , picture , her piano , the little worktable , and the beloved pussy .
Father 's best book find their way there , Mother 's easy chair , Jo 's desk , Amy 's fine sketch , and every day Meg bring her baby on a loving pilgrimage , to make sunshine for Aunty Beth .
John quietly set apart a little sum , that he might enjoy the pleasure of keep the invalid supply with the fruit she love and long for .
Old Hannah never weary of concoct dainty dish to tempt a capricious appetite , drop tear a she work , and from across the sea come little gift and cheerful letter , seem to bring breath of warmth and fragrance from land that know no winter .
Here , cherish like a household saint in it shrine , sit Beth , tranquil and busy a ever , for nothing could change the sweet , unselfish nature , and even while prepare to leave life , she try to make it happy for those who should remain behind .
The feeble finger be never idle , and one of her pleasure be to make little thing for the school child daily pass to and fro , to drop a pair of mitten from her window for a pair of purple hand , a needlebook for some small mother of many doll , penwipers for young penman toil through forest of pothook , scrapbook for picture-loving eye , and all manner of pleasant device , till the reluctant climber of the ladder of learn find their way strewn with flower , a it be , and come to regard the gentle giver a a sort of fairy godmother , who sit above there , and shower down gift miraculously suit to their taste and need .

The first few month be very happy one , and Beth often use to look round , and say `` How beautiful this be ! ''
a they all sit together in her sunny room , the baby kick and crow on the floor , mother and sister work near , and father reading , in his pleasant voice , from the wise old book which seem rich in good and comfortable word , a applicable now a when write century ago , a little chapel , where a paternal priest teach his flock the hard lesson all must learn , try to show them that hope can comfort love , and faith make resignation possible .
Simple sermon , that go straight to the soul of those who listen , for the father 's heart be in the minister 's religion , and the frequent falter in the voice give a double eloquence to the word he speak or read .
It be well for all that this peaceful time be give them a preparation for the sad hour to come , for by-and-by , Beth say the needle be ` so heavy ' , and put it down forever .

Ah me !

and to feel that there be no help .
A sad eclipse of the serene soul , a sharp struggle of the young life with death , but both be mercifully brief , and then the natural rebellion over , the old peace return more beautiful than ever .
With the wreck of her frail body , Beth 's soul grow strong , and though she say little , those about her felt that she be ready , saw that the first pilgrim call be likewise the fit , and wait with her on the shore , try to see the Shining Ones come to receive her when she cross the river .

She sleep on a couch in the room , wake often to renew the fire , to fee , lift , or wait upon the patient creature who seldom ask for anything , and ` try not to be a trouble ' .
All day she haunt the room , jealous of any other nurse , and prouder of be choose then than of any honor her life ever bring her .
Precious and helpful hour to Jo , for now her heart receive the teaching that it need .
Lessons in patience be so sweetly teach her that she could not fail to learn them , charity for all , the lovely spirit that can forgive and truly forget unkindness , the loyalty to duty that make the hard easy , and the sincere faith that fear nothing , but trust undoubtingly .
Often when she wake Jo find Beth reading in her well-worn little book , hear her sing softly , to beguile the sleepless night , or saw her lean her face upon her hand , while slow tear drop through the transparent finger , and Jo would lie watch her with thought too deep for tear , feel that Beth , in her simple , unselfish way , be try to wean herself from the dear old life , and fit herself for the life to come , by sacred word of comfort , quiet prayer , and the music she love so well .
Seeing this do more for Jo than the wise sermon , the saintliest hymn , the most fervent prayer that any voice could utter .
For with eye make clear by many tear , and a heart soften by the tenderest sorrow , she recognize the beauty of her sister 's life -- uneventful , unambitious , yet full of the genuine virtue which ` smell sweet , and blossom in the dust ' , the self-forgetfulness that make the humblest on earth remember soonest in heaven , the true success which be possible to all .
One night when Beth look among the book upon her table , to find something to make her forget the mortal weariness that be almost as hard to bear a pain , a she turn the leaf of her old favorite , Pilgrims 's Progress , she find a little paper , scribble over in Jo 's hand .

MY BETH Sitting patient in the shadow Till the blessed light shall come , A serene and saintly presence Sanctifies our troubled home .
Earthly joy and hope and sorrow Break like ripple on the strand Of the deep and solemn river Where her willing foot now stand .
O my sister , pass from me , Out of human care and strife , Leave me , a a gift , those virtue Which have beautify your life .
Dear , bequeath me that great patience Which have power to sustain A cheerful , uncomplaining spirit In it prison-house of pain .
Give me , for I need it sorely , Of that courage , wise and sweet , Which have make the path of duty Green beneath your willing foot .
Give me that unselfish nature , That with charity devine Can pardon wrong for love 's dear sake -- Meek heart , forgive me mine !
Thus our part daily loseth Something of it bitter pain , And while learn this hard lesson , My great loss becomes my gain .
For the touch of grief will render My wild nature more serene , Give to life new aspiration , A new trust in the unseen .
Henceforth , safe across the river , I shall see forever more A beloved , household spirit Waiting for me on the shore .
Hope and faith , born of my sorrow , Guardian angel shall become , And the sister go before me By their hand shall lead me home .
Blurred and blot , faulty and feeble a the line be , they bring a look of inexpressible comfort to Beth 's face , for her one regret have be that she have do so little , and this seem to assure her that her life have not be useless , that her death would not bring the despair she fear .

`` Not asleep , but so happy , dear .

she ask , with wistful , humble earnestness . ''

So the spring day come and go , the sky grow clear , the earth greener , the flower be up fairly early , and the bird come back in time to say goodbye to Beth , who , like a tired but trustful child , clung to the hand that have lead her all her life , a Father and Mother guide her tenderly through the Valley of the Shadow , and give her up to God .
Seldom except in book do the die utter memorable word , see vision , or depart with beatified countenance , and those who have speed many part soul know that to most the end come a naturally and simply a sleep .
As Beth have hop , the ` tide go out easily ' , and in the dark hour before dawn , on the bosom where she have draw her first breath , she quietly draw her last , with no farewell but one loving look , one little sigh .
With tear and prayer and tender hand , Mother and sister make her ready for the long sleep that pain would never mar again , see with grateful eye the beautiful serenity that soon replace the pathetic patience that have wring their heart so long , and feel with reverent joy that to their darling death be a benignant angel , not a phantom full of dread .
When morning come , for the first time in many month the fire be out , Jo 's place be empty , and the room be very still .
But a bird sang blithely on a budding bough , close by , the snowdrop blossom freshly at the window , and the spring sunshine stream in like a benediction over the placid face upon the pillow , a face so full of painless peace that those who love it best smile through their tear , and thank God that Beth be well at last .
CHAPTER FORTY-ONE LEARNING TO FORGET Amy 's lecture do Laurie good , though , of course , he do not own it till long afterward .
Men seldom do , for when woman be the adviser , the lord of creation do n't take the advice till they have persuade themselves that it be just what they intend to do .
Then they act upon it , and , if it succeed , they give the weak vessel half the credit of it .
If it fail , they generously give her the whole .

CHAPTER FORTY-TWO ALL ALONE It be easy to promise self-abnegation when self be wrap up in another , and heart and soul be purify by a sweet example .
But when the helpful voice be silent , the daily lesson over , the beloved presence go , and nothing remain but loneliness and grief , then Jo find her promise very hard to keep .
How could she ` comfort Father and Mother ' when her own heart ache with a ceaseless longing for her sister , how could she ` make the house cheerful ' when all it light and warmth and beauty seem to have desert it when Beth leave the old home for the new , and where in all the world could she ` find some useful , happy work to do ' , that would take the place of the loving service which have be it own reward ?
She try in a blind , hopeless way to do her duty , secretly rebel against it all the while , for it seem unjust that her few joy should be lessen , her burden make heavy , and life get hard and harder a she toil along .
Some people seem to get all sunshine , and some all shadow .
It be not fair , for she try more than Amy to be good , but never get any reward , only disappointment , trouble and hard work .
Poor Jo , these be dark day to her , for something like despair come over her when she think of spend all her life in that quiet house , devote to humdrum care , a few small pleasure , and the duty that never seem to grow any easy .
`` I ca n't do it .
I be n't mean for a life like this , and I know I shall break away and do something desperate if somebody do n't come and help me , '' she say to herself , when her first effort fail and she fell into the moody , miserable state of mind which often come when strong will have to yield to the inevitable .
But someone do come and help her , though Jo do not recognize her good angel at once because they wear familiar shape and use the simple spell best fit to poor humanity .
Often she start up at night , think Beth call her , and when the sight of the little empty bed make her cry with the bitter cry of unsubmissive sorrow , `` Oh , Beth , come back !
Come back ! ''
she do not stretch out her yearning arm in vain .
For , a quick to hear her sobbing a she have be to hear her sister 's faint whisper , her mother come to comfort her , not with word only , but the patient tenderness that soothe by a touch , tear that be mute reminder of a great grief than Jo 's , and broken whisper , more eloquent than prayer , because hopeful resignation go hand-in-hand with natural sorrow .
Sacred moment , when heart talk to heart in the silence of the night , turn affliction to a blessing , which chasten grief and strengthned love .
Feeling this , Jo 's burden seem easy to bear , duty grow sweeter , and life look more endurable , see from the safe shelter of her mother 's arm .
When ache heart be a little comforted , troubled mind likewise find help , for one day she go to the study , and lean over the good gray head lift to welcome her with a tranquil smile , she say very humbly , `` Father , talk to me a you do to Beth .
I need it more than she do , for I 'm all wrong . ''
`` My dear , nothing can comfort me like this , '' he answer , with a falter in his voice , and both arm round her , a if he too , need help , and do not fear to ask for it .
Then , sit in Beth 's little chair close beside him , Jo tell her trouble , the resentful sorrow for her loss , the fruitless effort that discourage her , the want of faith that make life look so dark , and all the sad bewilderment which we call despair .
She give him entire confidence , he give her the help she need , and both find consolation in the act .
For the time have come when they could talk together not only a father and daughter , but a man and woman , able and glad to serve each other with mutual sympathy as well a mutual love .

Brooms and dishcloth never could be as distasteful a they once have be , for Beth have preside over both , and something of her housewifely spirit seem to linger around the little mop and the old brush , never throw away .
As she use them , Jo find herself hum the song Beth use to hum , imitate Beth 's orderly way , and give the little touch here and there that keep everything fresh and cozy , which be the first step toward make home happy , though she do n't know it till Hannah say with an approve squeeze of the hand ... `` You thoughtful creeter , you 're determine we sha n't miss that dear lamb ef you can help it .

, always ` perwisin ' I could , '' say Jo , a she construct a kite for Demi in the topsy-turvy nursery .

She have often say she want to do something splendid , no matter how hard , and now she have her wish , for what could be more beautiful than to devote her life to Father and Mother , try to make home a happy to them a they have to her ?
And if difficulty be necessary to increase the splendor of the effort , what could be hard for a restless , ambitious girl than to give up her own hope , plan , and desire , and cheerfully live for others ?

CHAPTER FORTY-FIVE DAISY AND DEMI I can not feel that I have do my duty a humble historian of the March family , without devote at least one chapter to the two most precious and important member of it .
Daisy and Demi have now arrive at year of discretion , for in this fast age baby of three or four assert their right , and get them , too , which be more than many of their elder do .
If there ever be a pair of twin in danger of be utterly spoil by adoration , it be these prattle Brookes .
Of course they be the most remarkable child ever bear , a will be show when I mention that they walk at eight month , talk fluently at twelve month , and at two year they take their place at table , and behave with a propriety which charm all beholder .
At three , Daisy demand a ` needler ' , and actually make a bag with four stitch in it .
She likewise set up housekeeping in the sideboard , and manage a microscopic cook stove with a skill that bring tear of pride to Hannah 's eye , while Demi learn his letter with his grandfather , who invent a new mode of teach the alphabet by form letter with his arm and leg , thus unite gymnastics for head and heel .
The boy early develop a mechanical genius which delight his father and distract his mother , for he try to imitate every machine he saw , and keep the nursery in a chaotic condition , with his ` sewinsheen ' , a mysterious structure of string , chair , clothespin , and spool , for wheel to go ` wound and wind ' .
Also a basket hung over the back of a chair , in which he vainly try to hoist his too confide sister , who , with feminine devotion , allow her little head to be bump till rescue , when the young inventor indignantly remark , `` Why , Marmar , dat 's my lellywaiter , and me 's try to pull her up . ''
Though utterly unlike in character , the twin get on remarkably well together , and seldom quarrel more than thrice a day .
Of course , Demi tyrannize over Daisy , and gallantly defend her from every other aggressor , while Daisy make a galley slave of herself , and adore her brother a the one perfect be in the world .
A rosy , chubby , sunshiny little soul be Daisy , who find her way to everybody 's heart , and nestle there .
One of the captivating child , who seem make to be kiss and cuddle , adorn and adore like little goddess , and produce for general approval on all festive occasion .
Her small virtue be so sweet that she would have be quite angelic if a few small naughtiness have not keep her delightfully human .
It be all fair weather in her world , and every morning she scramble up to the window in her little nightgown to look out , and say , no matter whether it rain or shone , `` Oh , pitty day , oh , pitty day ! ''
Everyone be a friend , and she offer kiss to a stranger so confidingly that the most inveterate bachelor relent , and baby-lovers become faithful worshiper .
`` Me love evvybody , '' she once say , open her arm , with her spoon in one hand , and her mug in the other , a if eager to embrace and nourish the whole world .
As she grow , her mother begin to feel that the Dovecote would be bless by the presence of an inmate a serene and loving a that which have help to make the old house home , and to pray that she might be spar a loss like that which have lately teach them how long they have entertain an angel unawares .
Her grandfather often call her ` Beth ' , and her grandmother watch over her with untiring devotion , a if try to atone for some past mistake , which no eye but her own could see .
Demi , like a true Yankee , be of an inquire turn , want to know everything , and often get much disturb because he could not get satisfactory answer to his perpetual `` What for ? ''
He also possess a philosophic bent , to the great delight of his grandfather , who use to hold Socratic conversation with him , in which the precocious pupil occasionally pose his teacher , to the undisguised satisfaction of the womenfolk .
`` What make my legs go , Dranpa ? ''
ask the young philosopher , survey those active portion of his frame with a meditative air , while rest after a go-to-bed frolic one night .
`` It 's your little mind , Demi , '' reply the sage , stroke the yellow head respectfully .
`` What be a little mine ? ''
`` It be something which make your body move , a the spring make the wheel go in my watch when I show it to you . ''
`` Open me .
I want to see it go wound . ''
`` I ca n't do that any more than you could open the watch .
God wind you up , and you go till He stop you . ''
`` Does I ? ''
and Demi 's brown eye grow big and bright a he take in the new thought .
`` Is I wound up like the watch ? ''
`` Yes , but I ca n't show you how , for it be do when we do n't see . ''
Demi felt his back , a if expect to find it like that of the watch , and then gravely remark , `` I dess Dod do it when I 's asleep . ''
A careful explanation follow , to which he listen so attentively that his anxious grandmother say , `` My dear , do you think it wise to talk about such thing to that baby ?
He 's get great bump over his eye , and learn to ask the most unanswerable question . ''
`` If he be old enough to ask the question he be old enough to receive true answer .
I be not put the thought into his head , but help him unfold those already there .
These child be wise than we be , and I have no doubt the boy understand every word I have say to him .

If the boy have reply like Alcibiades , `` By the god , Socrates , I can not tell , '' his grandfather would not have be surprise , but when , after stand a moment on one leg , like a meditative young stork , he answer , in a tone of calm conviction , `` In my little belly , '' the old gentleman could only join in Grandma 's laugh , and dismiss the class in metaphysics .
There might have be cause for maternal anxiety , if Demi have not give convince proof that he be a true boy , as well a a budding philosopher , for often , after a discussion which cause Hannah to prophesy , with ominous nod , `` That child ai n't long for this world , '' he would turn about and set her fear at rest by some of the prank with which dear , dirty , naughty little rascal distract and delight their parent 's soul .
Meg make many moral rule , and try to keep them , but what mother be ever proof against the winning wile , the ingenious evasion , or the tranquil audacity of the miniature men and woman who so early show themselves accomplish Artful Dodgers ?
`` No more raisin , Demi .
They 'll make you sick , '' say Mamma to the young person who offer his service in the kitchen with unfailing regularity on plum-pudding day .
`` Me like to be sick . ''
`` I do n't want to have you , so run away and help Daisy make patty cake . ''
He reluctantly depart , but his wrong weigh upon his spirit , and by-and-by when an opportunity come to redress them , he outwit Mamma by a shrewd bargain .

`` Truly , Marmar ? ''

`` Yes , truly .
Anything you say , '' reply the shortsighted parent , prepare herself to sing , `` The Three Little Kittens '' half a dozen time over , or to take her family to `` Buy a penny bun , '' regardless of wind or limb .
But Demi corner her by the cool reply ... `` Then we 'll go and eat up all the raisin . ''
Aunt Dodo be chief playmate and confidante of both child , and the trio turn the little house topsy-turvy .
Aunt Amy be a yet only a name to them , Aunt Beth soon fade into a pleasantly vague memory , but Aunt Dodo be a living reality , and they make the most of her , for which compliment she be deeply grateful .
But when Mr. Bhaer come , Jo neglect her playfellow , and dismay and desolation fell upon their little soul .

Some person might have consider these please liberty a bribe , but Demi do n't see it in that light , and continue to patronize the ` the bear-man ' with pensive affability , while Daisy bestow her small affection upon him at the third call , and consider his shoulder her throne , his arm her refuge , his gifts treasure surpass worth .
Gentlemen be sometimes seize with sudden fit of admiration for the young relative of lady whom they honor with their regard , but this counterfeit philoprogenitiveness sits uneasily upon them , and do not deceive anybody a particle .
Mr. Bhaer 's devotion be sincere , however likewise effective -- for honesty be the best policy in love a in law .
He be one of the men who be at home with child , and look particularly well when little face make a pleasant contrast with his manly one .
His business , whatever it be , detain him from day to day , but even seldom fail to bring him out to see -- well , he always ask for Mr. March , so I suppose he be the attraction .
The excellent papa labor under the delusion that he be , and revel in long discussion with the kindred spirit , till a chance remark of his more observing grandson suddenly enlighten him .
Mr. Bhaer come in one evening to pause on the threshold of the study , astonish by the spectacle that meet his eye .

IN THE GARRET Four little chest all in a row , Dim with dust , and wear by time , All fashion and fill , long ago , By child now in their prime .
Four little key hang side by side , With faded ribbon , brave and gay When fasten there , with childish pride , Long ago , on a rainy day .
Four little names , one on each lid , Carved out by a boyish hand , And underneath there lieth hid Histories of the happy band Once play here , and pause oft To hear the sweet refrain , That come and go on the roof aloft , In the fall summer rain .
`` Meg '' on the first lid , smooth and fair .
I look in with loving eye , For fold here , with well-known care , A goodly gather lie , The record of a peaceful life -- Gifts to gentle child and girl , A bridal gown , line to a wife , A tiny shoe , a baby curl .
No toy in this first chest remain , For all be carry away , In their old age , to join again In another small Meg 's play .
Ah , happy mother !
Well I know You hear , like a sweet refrain , Lullabies ever soft and low In the fall summer rain .
`` Jo '' on the next lid , scratch and wear , And within a motley store Of headless doll , of schoolbook tear , Birds and beast that speak no more , Spoils bring home from the fairy ground Only trod by youthful foot , Dreams of a future never find , Memories of a past still sweet , Half-writ poem , story wild , April letter , warm and cold , Diaries of a wilful child , Hints of a woman early old , A woman in a lonely home , Hearing , like a sad refrain -- `` Be worthy , love , and love will come , '' In the fall summer rain .
My Beth !
the dust be always sweep From the lid that bear your name , As if by love eye that weep , By careful hand that often come .
Death canonize for u one saint , Ever less human than divine , And still we lay , with tender plaint , Relics in this household shrine -- The silver bell , so seldom rung , The little cap which last she wear , The fair , dead Catherine that hung By angel borne above her door .
The song she sing , without lament , In her prison-house of pain , Forever be they sweetly blent With the fall summer rain .
Upon the last lid 's polished field -- Legend now both fair and true A gallant knight bear on his shield , `` Amy '' in letter gold and blue .
Within lie snood that bind her hair , Slippers that have dance their last , Faded flower lay by with care , Fans whose airy toil be past , Gay valentine , all ardent flame , Trifles that have bear their part In girlish hope and fear and shame , The record of a maiden heart Now learn fairer , truer spell , Hearing , like a blithe refrain , The silver sound of bridal bell In the fall summer rain .
Four little chest all in a row , Dim with dust , and wear by time , Four woman , teach by weal and woe To love and labor in their prime .
Four sister , part for an hour , None lose , one only go before , Made by love 's immortal power , Nearest and dear evermore .
Oh , when these hidden store of ours Lie open to the Father 's sight , May they be rich in golden hour , Deeds that show fairer for the light , Lives whose brave music long shall ring , Like a spirit-stirring strain , Souls that shall gladly soar and sing In the long sunshine after rain .

CHAPTER FORTY-SEVEN HARVEST TIME For a year Jo and her Professor worked and wait , hop and love , meet occasionally , and write such voluminous letter that the rise in the price of paper be account for , Laurie say .
