MARJORIE 'S THREE GIFTS Marjorie sit on the door-step , shell pea , quite unconscious what a pretty picture she make , with the rose peep at her through the lattice work of the porch , the wind play hide-and-seek in her curly hair , while the sunshine with it silent magic change her fade gingham to a golden gown , and shimmer on the bright tin pan a if it be a silver shield .
Old Rover lay at her foot , the white kitten purr on her shoulder , and friendly robin hop about her in the grass , chirp `` A happy birthday , Marjorie ! ''
But the little maid neither saw nor heard , for her eye be fix on the green pod , and her thought be far away .
She be recall the fairy-tale granny tell her last night , and wish with all her heart that such thing happen nowadays .
For in this story , a a poor girl like herself sit spin before the door , a Brownie come by , and give the child a good-luck penny ; then a fairy pass , and leave a talisman which would keep her always happy ; and last of all , the prince roll up in his chariot , and take her away to reign with him over a lovely kingdom , a a reward for her many kindness to others .
When Marjorie imagine this part of the story , it be impossible to help give one little sigh , and for a minute she forget her work , so busy be she think what beautiful present she would give to all the poor child in her realm when THEY have birthday .
Five impatient young pea take this opportunity to escape from the half-open pod in her hand and skip down the step , to be immediately gobble up by an audacious robin , who give thanks in such a shrill chirp that Marjorie wake up , laugh , and fell to work again .
She be just finishing , when a voice call out from the lane , -- `` Hi , there !
come here a minute , child ! ''
and look up , she saw a little old man in a queer little carriage draw by a fat little pony .

`` But vacation be play-time , -- how about that ? ''
`` Why , that sort of work IS play , and I get bit of fun all along .
I always have a good swing when I go for the cow , and pick flower with the dandelion .
Weeding be n't so nice , but berry be very pleasant , and we have good time all together . ''
`` What shall you do with your money when you get it ? ''
`` Oh , lot of thing !
Buy book and clothes for school , and , if I get a great deal , give some to granny .
I 'd love to do that , for she take care of me , and I 'd be so proud to help her ! ''
`` Good little lass ! ''
say the old gentleman , a he put his hand in his pocket .

he add , apparently address himself to a large frog who sit upon a stone , look so wise and grandfatherly that it really do seem quite proper to consult him .
At all event , he give his opinion in the most decided manner , for , with a loud croak , he turn an undignified somersault into the brook , splash up the water at a great rate .
`` Well , perhaps it would n't be best on the whole .
Industry be a good teacher , and money can not buy happiness , a I know to my sorrow . ''

`` Now come and see what I be do , '' say the lady , when she have thank the child .
Marjorie draw near confidingly , and look down at the wide-spread book before her .
She give a start , and laugh out with surprise and delight ; for there be a lovely picture of her own little home , and her own little self on the door-step , all so delicate , and beautiful , and true , it seem a if do by magic .
`` Oh , how pretty !
There be Rover , and Kitty and the robin , and me !
How could you ever do it , ma'am ? ''
say Marjorie , with a wonder glance at the long paint-brush , which have work what seem a miracle to her childish eye .
`` I 'll show you presently ; but tell me , first , if it look quite right and natural to you .
Children sometimes spy out fault that no one else can see , '' answer the lady , evidently please with the artless praise her work receive .
`` It look just like our house , only more beautiful .
Perhaps that be because I know how shabby it really be .
That moss look lovely on the shingle , but the roof leak .
The porch be break , only the rose hide the place ; and my gown be all faded , though it once be as bright a you have make it .
I wish the house and everything would stay pretty forever , a they will in the picture . ''
While Marjorie speak , the lady have be add more color to the sketch , and when she look up , something warmer and brighter than sunshine shone in her face , a she say , so cheerily , it be like a bird 's song to hear her , -- `` It ca n't be summer always , dear , but we can make fair weather for ourselves if we try .
The moss , the rose , and soft shadow show the little house and the little girl at their best , and that be what we all should do ; for it be amazing how lovely common thing become , if one only know how to look at them . ''
`` I wish I do , '' say Marjorie , half to herself , remember how often she be discontent , and how hard it be to get on , sometimes .
`` So do I , '' say the lady , in her happy voice .
`` Just believe that there be a sunny side to everything , and try to find it , and you will be surprise to see how bright the world will seem , and how cheerful you will be able to keep your little self . ''
`` I guess granny have find that out , for she never fret .
I do , but I 'm go to stop it , because I 'm twelve to-day , and that be too old for such thing , '' say Marjorie , recollect the good resolution she have make that morning when she wake .
`` I be twice twelve , and not entirely cure yet ; but I try , and do n't mean to wear blue spectacle if I can help it , '' answer the lady , laugh so blithely that Marjorie be sure she would not have to try much longer .
`` Birthdays be make for present , and I should like to give you one .
Would it please you to have this little picture ? ''
she add , lift it out of the book .
`` Truly my own ?
Oh , yes , indeed ! ''
cry Marjorie , color with pleasure , for she have never own so beautiful a thing before .
`` Then you shall have it , dear .
Hang it where you can see it often , and when you look , remember that it be the sunny side of home , and help to keep it so . ''
Marjorie have nothing but a kiss to offer by way of thanks , a the lovely sketch be put into her hand ; but the giver seem quite satisfied , for it be a very grateful little kiss .
Then the child take up her basket and go away , not dance and sing now , but slowly and silently ; for this gift make her thoughtful as well a glad .
As she climb the wall , she look back to nod good-by to the pretty lady ; but the meadow be empty , and all she saw be the grass blowing in the wind .
`` Now , deary , run out and play , for birthday come but once a year , and we must make them as merry a we can , '' say granny , a she settle herself for her afternoon nap , when the Saturday cleaning be all do , and the little house as neat a wax .
So Marjorie put on a white apron in honor of the occasion , and , take Kitty in her arm , go out to enjoy herself .
Three swing on the gate seem to be a good way of begin the festivity ; but she only get two , for when the gate creak back the second time , it stay shut , and Marjorie hung over the picket , arrest by the sound of music .
`` It 's soldier , '' she say , a the fife and drum draw nearer , and flag be see wave over the barberry-bushes at the corner .
`` No ; it 's a picnic , '' she add in a moment ; for she saw hat with wreath about them bob up and down , a a gayly-trimmed hay-cart full of child come rumble down the lane .
`` What a nice time they be go to have ! ''
think Marjorie , sadly contrast that merry-making with the quiet party she be have all by herself .
Suddenly her face shone , and Kitty be wave over her head like a banner , a she fly out of the gate , cry , rapturously , -- `` It 's Billy !
and I know he 's come for me ! ''
It certainly WAS Billy , proudly drive the old horse , and beam at his little friend from the bower of flag and chestnut-boughs , where he sit in state , with a crown of daisy on his sailor-hat and a spray of bloom sweetbrier in his hand .
Waving his rustic sceptre , he lead off the shout of `` Happy birthday , Marjorie ! ''
which be set up a the wagon stop at the gate , and the green boughs suddenly blossom with familiar face , all smile on the little damsel , who stand in the lane quite overpower with delight .
`` It 's a s ` prise party ! ''
cry one small lad , tumble out behind .
`` We be go up the mountain to have fun ! ''
add a chorus of voice , a a dozen hand beckon wildly .
`` We get it up on purpose for you , so tie your hat and come away , '' say a pretty girl , lean down to kiss Marjorie , who have drop Kitty , and stand ready for any splendid enterprise .
A word to granny , and away go the happy child , sit up beside Billy , under the flag that wave over a happy load than any royal chariot ever bore .
It would be vain to try and tell all the play and pleasure of happy child on a Saturday afternoon , but we may briefly say that Marjorie find a mossy stone all ready for her throne , and Billy crown her with a garland like his own .
That a fine banquet be spread , and eaten with a relish many a Lord Mayor 's feast have lack .
Then how the whole court dance and play together afterward !
The lord climb tree and turn somersault , the lady gather flower and tell secret under the sweetfern-bushes , the queen lose her shoe jumping over the waterfall , and the king paddle into the pool below and rescue it .
A happy little kingdom , full of summer sunshine , innocent delight , and loyal heart ; for love rule , and the only war that disturb the peaceful land be wag by the mosquito a night come on .
Marjorie stand on her throne watch the sunset while her maid of honor pack up the remains of the banquet , and her knight prepare the chariot .
All the sky be gold and purple , all the world bath in a soft , red light , and the little girl be very happy a she look down at the subject who have serve her so faithfully that day .
`` Have you have a good time , Marjy ? ''
ask King William ; who stand below , with his royal nose on a level with her majesty 's two dusty little shoe .
`` Oh , Billy , it have be just splendid !
But I do n't see why you should all be so kind to me , '' answer Marjorie , with such a look of innocent wonder , that Billy laugh to see it .
`` Because you be so sweet and good , we ca n't help love you , -- that 's why , '' he say , a if this simple fact be reason enough .
`` I 'm go to be the best girl that ever be , and love everybody in the world , '' cry the child , stretch out her arm a if ready , in the fulness of her happy heart , to embrace all creation .
`` Do n't turn into an angel and fly away just yet , but come home , or granny will never lend you to u any more . ''
With that , Billy jump her down , and away they run , to ride gayly back through the twilight , sing like a flock of nightingale .
As she go to bed that night , Marjorie look at the red bank , the pretty picture , and the daisy crown , say to herself , -- `` It have be a VERY nice birthday , and I be something like the girl in the story , after all , for the old man give me a good-luck penny , the kind lady tell me how to keep happy , and Billy come for me like the prince .
The girl do n't go back to the poor house again , but I 'm glad I do , for MY granny be n't a cross one , and my little home be the dearest in the world . ''
Then she tie her night-cap , say her prayer , and fell asleep ; but the moon , look in to kiss the blooming face upon the pillow , know that three good spirit have come to help little Marjorie from that day forth , and their name be Industry , Cheerfulness , and Love .
ROSES AND FORGET-ME-NOTS I . ROSES It be a cold November storm , and everything look forlorn .
Even the pert sparrow be draggle-tailed and too much out of spirit to fight for crumb with the fat pigeon who trip through the mud with their little red boot a if in haste to get back to their cosy home in the dove-cot .
But the most forlorn creature out that day be a small errand girl , with a bonnet-box on each arm , and both hand struggle to hold a big broken umbrella .
A pair of worn-out boot let in the wet upon her tired foot ; a thin cotton dress and an old shawl poorly protect her from the storm ; and a faded hood cover her head .
The face that look out from this hood be too pale and anxious for one so young ; and when a sudden gust turn the old umbrella inside out with a crash , despair fell upon poor Lizzie , and she be so miserable she could have sit down in the rain and cry .
But there be no time for tear ; so , drag the dilapidated umbrella along , she spread her shawl over the bonnet-boxes and hurry down the broad street , eager to hide her misfortune from a pretty young girl who stand at a window laughing at her .
She could not find the number of the house where one of the fine hat be to be leave ; and after hunt all down one side of the street , she cross over , and come at last to the very house where the pretty girl live .
She be no long to be see ; and , with a sigh of relief , Lizzie ring the bell , and be tell to wait in the hall while Miss Belle try the hat on .
Glad to rest , she warm her foot , right her umbrella , and then sit look about her with eye quick to see the beauty and the comfort that make the place so homelike and delightful .
A small waiting-room open from the hall , and in it stand many blooming plant , whose fragrance attract Lizzie as irresistibly a if she have be a butterfly or bee .
Slipping in , she stand enjoy the lovely color , sweet odor , and delicate shape of these household spirit ; for Lizzie love flower passionately ; and just then they possess a peculiar charm for her .
One particularly captivate little rise win her heart , and make her long for it with a longing that become a temptation too strong to resist .
It be so perfect ; so like a rosy face smile out from the green leaf , that Lizzie could NOT keep her hand off it , and have smelt , touch , and kiss it , she suddenly break the stem and hid it in her pocket .
Then , frighten at what she have do , she creep back to her place in the hall , and sit there , burden with remorse .
A servant come just then to lead her upstairs ; for Miss Belle wish the hat alter , and must give direction .
With her heart in a flutter , and pinker rose in her cheek than the one in her pocket , Lizzie follow to a handsome room , where a pretty girl stand before a long mirror with the hat in her hand .
`` Tell Madame Tifany that I do n't like it at all , for she have n't put in the blue plume mamma order ; and I wo n't have rose-buds , they be so common , '' say the young lady , in a dissatisfied tone , a she twirl the hat about .
`` Yes , miss , '' be all Lizzie could say ; for SHE consider that hat the lovely thing a girl could possibly own .
`` You have good ask your mamma about it , Miss Belle , before you give any order .
She will be up in a few moment , and the girl can wait , '' put in a maid , who be sew in the ante-room .
`` I suppose I must ; but I WO N'T have rose , '' answer Belle , crossly .
Then she glance at Lizzie , and say more gently , `` You look very cold ; come and sit by the fire while you wait . ''
`` I 'm afraid I 'll wet the pretty rug , miss ; my foot be sop , '' say Lizzie , gratefully , but timidly .
`` So they be !
Why do n't you wear rubber boot ? ''
`` I have n't get any . ''
`` I 'll give you mine , then , for I hate them ; and a I never go out in wet weather , they be of no earthly use to me .
Marie , bring them here ; I shall be glad to get rid of them , and I 'm sure they 'll be useful to you . ''
`` Oh , thank you , miss !
I 'd like 'em ever so much , for I 'm out in the rain half the time , and get bad cold because my boot be old , '' say Lizzie , smile brightly at the thought of the welcome gift .
`` I should think your mother would get you warm thing , '' begin Belle , who find something rather interesting in the shabby girl , with shy bright eye , and curly hair burst out of the old hood .
`` I have n't get any mother , '' say Lizzie , with a pathetic glance at her poor clothes .
`` I 'm so sorry !
Have you brother and sister ? ''
ask Belle , hop to find something pleasant to talk about ; for she be a kind little soul .
`` No , miss ; I 've get no folk at all . ''
`` Oh , dear ; how sad !
Why , who take care of you ? ''
cry Belle , look quite distress .
`` No one ; I take care of myself .
I work for Madame , and she pay me a dollar a week .
I stay with Mrs. Brown , and chore round to pay for my keep .
My dollar do n't get many clothes , so I ca n't be as neat a I 'd like . ''
And the forlorn look come back to poor Lizzie 's face .
Belle say nothing , but sit among the sofa cushion , where she have throw herself , look soberly at this other girl , no old than she be , who take care of herself and be all alone in the world .
It be a new idea to Belle , who be love and pet a an only child be apt to be .
She often saw beggar and pity them , but know very little about their want and live ; so it be like turn a new page in her happy life to be bring so near to poverty a this chance meeting with the milliner 's girl .
`` Are n't you afraid and lonely and unhappy ? ''
she say , slowly , try to understand and put herself in Lizzie 's place .
`` Yes ; but it 's no use .
I ca n't help it , and may be thing will get good by and by , and I 'll have my wish , '' answer Lizzie , more hopefully , because Belle 's pity warm her heart and make her trouble seem light .
`` What be your wish ? ''
ask Belle , hop mamma would n't come just yet , for she be get interested in the stranger .
`` To have a nice little room , and make flower , like a French girl I know .
It 's such pretty work , and she get lot of money , for every one like her flower .
She show me how , sometimes , and I can do leaf first-rate ; but -- '' There Lizzie stop suddenly , and the color rush up to her forehead ; for she remember the little rise in her pocket and it weigh upon her conscience like a stone .
Before Belle could ask what be the matter , Marie come in with a tray of cake and fruit , say : `` Here 's your lunch , Miss Belle . ''
`` Put it down , please ; I 'm not ready for it yet . ''
And Belle shake her head a she glance at Lizzie , who be star hard at the fire with such a troubled face that Belle could not bear to see it .
Jumping out of her nest of cushion , she heap a plate with good thing , and go to Lizzie , offer it , say , with a gentle courtesy that make the act doubly sweet : `` Please have some ; you must be tire of wait . ''
But Lizzie could not take it ; she could only cover her face and cry ; for this kindness rent her heart and make the steal flower a burden too heavy to be borne .
`` Oh , do n't cry so !
Are you sick ?
Have I be rude ?
Tell me all about it ; and if I ca n't do anything , mamma can , '' say Belle , surprise and trouble .
`` No ; I 'm not sick ; I 'm bad , and I ca n't bear it when you be so good to me , '' sob Lizzie , quite overcome with penitence ; and take out the crumpled rise , she confess her fault with many tear .
`` Do n't feel so much about such a little thing a that , '' begin Belle , warmly ; then check herself , and add , more soberly , `` It WAS wrong to take it without leave ; but it 's all right now , and I 'll give you a many rose a you want , for I know you be a good girl . ''
`` Thank you .
I do n't want it only because it be pretty , but I want to copy it .
I ca n't get any for myself , and so I ca n't do my make-believe one well .
Madame wo n't even lend me the old one in the store , and Estelle have none to spare for me , because I ca n't pay her for teach me .
She give me bit of muslin and wire and thing , and show me now and then .
But I know if I have a real flower I could copy it ; so she 'd see I do know something , for I try real hard .
I 'm SO tired of slop round the street , I 'd do anything to earn my living some other way . ''
Lizzie have pour out her trouble rapidly ; and the little story be quite affect when one saw the tear on her cheek , the poor clothes , and the thin hand that hold the steal rise .
Belle be much touch , and , in her impetuous way , set about mend matter as fast a possible .
`` Put on those boot and that pair of dry stocking right away .
Then tuck as much cake and fruit into your pocket a it will hold .
I 'm go to get you some flower , and see if mamma be too busy to attend to me . ''
With a nod and a smile , Belle fly about the room a minute ; then vanish , leave Lizzie to her comfortable task , feel a if fairy still haunt the world a in the good old time .
When Belle come back with a handful of rose , she find Lizzie absorb in admire contemplation of her new boot , a she eat sponge-cake in a blissful sort of waking-dream .
`` Mamma ca n't come ; but I do n't care about the hat .
It will do very well , and be n't worth fuss about .
There , will those be of any use to you ? ''
And she offer the nosegay with a much happy face than the one Lizzie first saw .
`` Oh , miss , they 're just lovely !
I 'll copy that pink rise as soon a ever I can , and when I 've learn how to do 'em tip-top , I 'd like to bring you some , if you do n't mind , '' answer Lizzie , smile all over her face a she bury her nose luxuriously in the fragrant mass .
`` I 'd like it very much , for I should think you 'd have to be very clever to make such pretty thing .
I really quite fancy those rosebud in my hat , now I know that you 're go to learn how to make them .
Put an orange in your pocket , and the flower in water as soon a you can , so they 'll be fresh when you want them .
Good-by .
Bring home our hat every time and tell me how you get on . ''
With kind word like these , Belle dismiss Lizzie , who run downstairs , feel as rich a if she have find a fortune .
Away to the next place she hurry , anxious to get her errand do and the precious posy safely into fresh water .
But Mrs. Turretviile be not at home , and the bonnet could not be leave till pay for .
So Lizzie turn to go down the high step , glad that she need not wait .
She stop one instant to take a delicious sniff at her flower , and that be the last happy moment that poor Lizzie know for many weary month .
The new boot be large for her , the step slippery with sleet , and down go the little errand girl , from top to bottom , till she land in the gutter directly upon Mrs. Turretville 's costly bonnet .
`` I 've save my posy , anyway , '' sigh Lizzie , a she pick herself up , bruise , wet , and faint with pain ; `` but , oh , my heart !
wo n't Madame scold when she see that band-box smash flat , '' groan the poor child , sit on the curbstone to get her breath and view the disaster .
The rain pour , the wind blew , the sparrow on the park rail chirp derisively , and no one come along to help Lizzie out of her trouble .
Slowly she gather up her burden ; painfully she limp away in the big boot ; and the last the naughty sparrow saw of her be a shabby little figure go round the corner , with a pale , tearful face hold lovingly over the bright bouquet that be her one treasure and her only comfort in the moment which bring to her the great misfortune of her life .
II .
FORGET-ME-NOTS `` Oh , mamma , I be so relieved that the box have come at last !
If it have not , I do believe I should have die of disappointment , '' cry pretty Belle , five year later , on the morning before her eighteenth birthday .
`` It would have be a serious disappointment , darling ; for I have sot my heart on your wear my gift to-morrow night , and when the steamer keep come in without my trunk from Paris , I be very anxious .
I hope you will like it . ''
`` Dear mamma , I know I shall like it ; your taste be so good and you know what suit me so well .
Make haste , Marie ; I 'm die to see it , '' say Belle , dance about the great trunk , a the maid carefully unfolded tissue paper and muslin wrapper .
A young girl 's first ball-dress be a grand affair , -- in her eye , at least ; and Belle soon stop dance , to stand with clasped hand , eager eye and part lip before the snowy pile of illusion that be at last daintily lift out upon the bed .
Then , a Marie display it loveliness , little cry of delight be hear , and when the whole delicate dress be arrange to the best effect she throw herself upon her mother 's neck and actually cry with pleasure .
`` Mamma , it be too lovely I and you be very kind to do so much for me .
How shall I ever thank you ? ''
`` By put it right on to see if it fit ; and when you wear it look your happy , that I may be proud of my pretty daughter . ''
Mamma get no further , for Marie utter a French shriek , wring her hand , and then begin to burrow wildly in the trunk and among the paper , cry distractedly : `` Great Heavens , madame !
the wreath have be forget !
What an affliction !
Mademoiselle 's enchant toilette be destroy without the wreath , and nowhere do I find it . ''
In vain they search ; in vain Marie wail and Belle declare it must be somewhere ; no wreath appear .
It be duly set down in the bill , and a fine sum charge for a head-dress to match the dainty forget-me-not that loop the fleecy skirt and ornament the bosom of the dress .
It have evidently be forget ; and mamma despatch Marie at once to try and match the flower , for Belle would not hear of any other decoration for her beautiful blonde hair .
The dress fit to a charm , and be pronounce by all beholder the lovely thing ever see .
Nothing be want but the wreath to make it quite perfect , and when Marie return , after a long search , with no forget-me-not , Belle be in despair .
`` Wear natural one , '' suggest a sympathizing friend .
But another hunt among greenhouse be as fruitless a that among the milliner ' room .
No forget-me-not could be find , and Marie fell exhaust into a chair , desolate at what she felt to be an awful calamity .
`` Let me have the carriage , and I 'll ransack the city till I find some , '' cry Belle , grow more resolute with each failure .
Marnma be deep in preparation for the ball , and could not help her afflicted daughter , though she be much disappoint at the mishap .
So Belle drive off , resolve to have her flower whether there be any or not .
Any one who have ever try to match a ribbon , find a certain fabric , or get anything do in a hurry , know what a wearisome task it sometimes be , and can imagine Belle 's state of mind after repeat disappointment .
She be about to give up in despair , when some one suggest that perhaps the Frenchwoman , Estelle Valnor , might make the desired wreath , if there be time .
Away drove Belle , and , on enter the room , give a sigh of satisfaction , for a whole boxful of the lovely forget-me-nots stood upon the table .
As fast a possible , she tell her tale and demand the flower , no matter what the price might be .
Imagine her feeling when the Frenchwoman , with a shrug , announce that it be impossible to give mademoiselle a single spray .
All be engage to trim a bridesmaid 's dress , and must be send away at once .
It really be too bad !
and Belle lose her temper entirely , for no persuasion or bribe would win a spray from Estelle .
The provoke part of it be that the wedding would not come off for several day , and there be time enough to make more flower for that dress , since Belle only want a few for her hair .
Neither would Estelle make her any , a her hand be full , and so small an order be not worth derange one 's self for ; but observe Belle 's sorrowful face , she say , affably : `` Mademoiselle may , perhaps , find the flower she desire at Miss Berton 's .
She have be help me with these garland , and may have some left .
Here be her address . ''
Belle take the card with thanks , and hurry away with a last hope faintly stir in her girlish heart , for Belle have an unusually ardent wish to look her best at this party , since Somebody be to be there , and Somebody consider forget-me-nots the sweet flower in the world .
Mamma know this , and the kiss Belle give her when the dress come have a more tender meaning than gratified vanity or daughterly love .
Up many stair she climb , and come at last to a little room , very poor but very neat , where , at the one window , sit a young girl , with crutch by her side and her lap full of flower-leaves and petal .
She rise slowly a Belle come in , and then stand look at her , with such a wistful expression in her shy , bright eye , that Belle 's anxious face clear involuntarily , and her voice lose it impatient tone .
As she speak , she glance about the room , hop to see some blue blossom await her .
But none appear ; and she be about to despond again , when the girl say , gently : `` I have none by me now , but I may be able to find you some . ''
`` Thank you very much ; but I have be everywhere in vain .
Still , if you do get any , please send them to me as soon a possible .
Here be my card . ''
Miss Berton glance at it , then cast a quick look at the sweet , anxious face before her , and smile so brightly that Belle smile also , and ask , wonderingly : `` What be it ?
What do you see ? ''
`` I see the dear young lady who be so kind to me long ago .
You do n't remember me , and never know my name ; but I never have forget you all these year .
I always hop I could do something to show how grateful I be , and now I can , for you shall have your flower if I sit up all night to make them . ''
But Belle still shake her head and watch the smile face before her with wondering eye , till the girl add , with sudden color in her cheek : `` Ah , you 've do so many kind thing in your life , you do n't remember the little errand girl from Madame Tifany 's who steal a rise in your hall , and how you give her rubber boot and cake and flower , and be so good to her she could n't forget it if she live to be a hundred . ''
`` But you be so change , '' begin Belle , who do faintly recollect that little incident in her happy life .
`` Yes , I have a fall and hurt myself so that I shall always be lame . ''
And Lizzie go on to tell how Madame have dismiss her in a rage ; how she lay ill till Mrs. Brown send her to the hospital ; and how for a year she have suffer much alone , in that great house of pain , before one of the kind visitor have befriend her .
While hear the story of the five year , that have be so full of pleasure , ease and love for herself , Belle forget her errand , and , sit beside Lizzie , listen with pity eye to all she tell of her endeavor to support herself by the delicate handiwork she love .
`` I 'm very happy now , '' end Lizzie , look about the little bare room with a face full of the sweet content .
`` I get nearly work enough to pay my way , and Estelle send me some when she have more than she can do .
I 've learn to do it nicely , and it be so pleasant to sit here and make flower instead of trudge about in the wet with other people 's hat .
Though I do sometimes wish I be able to trudge , one get on so slowly with crutch . ''
A little sigh follow the word , and Belle put her own plump hand on the delicate one that hold the crutch , say , in her cordial young voice : `` I 'll come and take you to drive sometimes , for you be too pale , and you 'll get ill sit here at work day after day .
Please let me ; I 'd love to ; for I feel so idle and wicked when I see busy people like you that I reproach myself for neglect my duty and have more than my share of happiness . ''
Lizzie thank her with a look , and then say , in a tone of interest that be delightful to hear : `` Tell about the wreath you want ; I should so love to do it for you , if I can . ''
Belle have forget all about it in listen to this sad little story of a girl 's life .
Now she felt half ashamed to talk of so frivolous a matter till she remember that it would help Lizzie ; and , resolve to pay for it a never garland be pay for before , she enter upon the subject with renew interest .
`` You shall have the flower in time for your ball to-morrow night .
I will engage to make a wreath that will please you , only it may take long than I think .
Do n't be trouble if I do n't send it till even ; it will surely come in time .
I can work fast , and this will be the happy job I ever do , '' say Lizzie , begin to lay out mysterious little tool and bend delicate wire .
`` You be altogether too grateful for the little I have do .
It make me feel ashamed to think I do not find you out before and do something well worth thanks . ''
`` Ah , it be n't the boot or the cake or the rose , dear Miss Belle .
It be the kind look , the gentle word , the way it be do , that go right to my heart , and do me more good than a million of money .
I never steal a pin after that day , for the little rise would n't let me forget how you forgive me so sweetly .
I sometimes think it keep me from great temptation , for I be a poor , forlorn child , with no one to keep me good . ''
Pretty Belle look pretty than ever a she listen , and a bright tear stand in either eye like a drop of dew on a blue flower .
It touch her very much to learn that her little act of childish charity have be so sweet and helpful to this lonely girl , and now live so freshly in her grateful memory .
It show her , suddenly , how precious little deed of love and sympathy be ; how strong to bless , how easy to perform , how comfortable to recall .
Her heart be very full and tender just then , and the lesson sunk deep into it never to be forget .
She sit a long time watch flower bud and blossom under Lizzie 's skilful finger , and then hurry home to tell all her glad news to mamma .
If the next day have not be full of most delightfully exciting event , Belle might have felt some anxiety about her wreath , for hour after hour go by and nothing arrive from Lizzie .
Evening come , and all be ready .
Belle be dress , and look so lovely that mamma declare she need nothing more .

Seventeen year of silence , seventeen year of secret dread and remorse for me , '' she say , pace the room with tightly lock hand and eye full of unspeakable anguish .
`` Oh , Richard , Richard !
I forgive you long ago , and surely I have expiate my innocent offense by these year of suffering !
For her sake I do it , and for her sake I still keep dumb .
God know I ask nothing for myself but rest and oblivion by your side . ''
Half an hour later , Paul stand at the hall door .
It be ajar , for the family have return unexpectedly , a be evident from the open door and empty hall .
Entering unseen , he ascend to the room my lady usually occupy .
The fire burn low , Lillian 's chair be empty , and my lady lay asleep , a if lull by the sigh wind without and the deep silence that reign within .
Paul stand regard her with a great pity soften his face a he mark the sunken eye , pallid cheek , lock too early gray , and restless lip mutter in dream .
`` I wish I could spare her this , '' he sigh , stoop to wake her with a word .
